## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv_dt depends on position x (restoring force), velocity v (damping), and time t (possible external driving). The physics is governed by Newton's second law with nonlinear force terms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (with periodic driving)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (full Duffing equation)
- Quintic nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order nonlinearity)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * abs(v) (quadratic velocity damping)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * x (time-modulated stiffness)
- Cubic damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (nonlinear velocity-dependent force)
- Mixed nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**2 * v + c3 * v (position-velocity coupling)
- Helmholtz oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (quadratic nonlinear restoring force)
- General polynomial force: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (combined nonlinearities)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium, while even powers (x**2) break symmetry — choose based on observed trajectory symmetry
- Velocity-dependent terms linear in v indicate viscous damping; terms like v*x**2 indicate amplitude-dependent damping (Van der Pol type)
- Sinusoidal time dependence sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) in acceleration indicates external periodic driving force
- If the system shows limit cycles, look for nonlinear damping structures like (1 - c*x**2)*v where damping sign changes with amplitude
- Position-velocity product terms like x*v arise from forces that depend on both displacement and rate, common in nonlinear friction models
- Absence of explicit time dependence suggests an autonomous system where energy considerations (conservative + dissipative) fully determine dynamics
- Rational restoring forces like x/(1 + c*x**2) model softening springs with bounded force at large displacements
- Phase-space structure (x,v trajectories) spiraling inward implies net dissipation; use odd powers of v for symmetric damping

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.0230405406738805*v**3 - 1.1056075693807*x*(0.0552411020531317*Abs(v)**0.333333333333333 + 1) - 1.1056075693807*x + 0.350781823399691*sin(t)`

Let me expand this:
- `-0.0230405406738805*v**3`
- `-1.1056075693807*x*0.0552411020531317*Abs(v)**(1/3) - 1.1056075693807*x`
- `-1.1056075693807*x`
- `+0.350781823399691*sin(t)`

So GT = `-2.2112151387614*x - 0.0610764910802*x*Abs(v)**(1/3) - 0.0230405406738805*v**3 + 0.350781823399691*sin(t)`

The GT has these basis functions:
1. `x` (linear)
2. `x*Abs(v)**(1/3)`
3. `v**3`
4. `sin(t)`

Note: `sin(t)` can be written as `cos(t + c)` with appropriate phase shift (c = -π/2).

Now I'll check each candidate for whether it can match these four terms exactly (with no extra non-eliminable terms).

For a candidate to match, it must:
- Have terms proportional to `x`, `x*Abs(v)**(1/3)`, `v**3`, and `sin(t)` (or `cos(t+c)`)
- Any extra terms must be eliminable (by setting coefficients to 0)

Let me go through each candidate:

Has extra `v` term. Set c6=0. Has `Abs(v)**c2` with free c2, set c2=1/3. `cos(c5+t)` matches `sin(t)` with c5=π/2. ✓
